<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Form in which people experience and express themselves sexually</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This article is about human sexual anatomy, sexuality and perceptions. For information specifically about sexual activities, see <a href="/wiki/Human_sexual_activity" title="Human sexual activity">Human sexual activity</a>. For the book, see <a href="/wiki/Human_Sexuality_(book)" title="Human Sexuality (book)">Human Sexuality (book)</a>.</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Sexuality" redirects here. For sexual behavior among other animals, see <a href="/wiki/Animal_sexual_behaviour" title="Animal sexual behaviour">Animal sexual behaviour</a>. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Sexuality_(disambiguation)" title="Sexuality (disambiguation)">Sexuality (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<p><b>Human sexuality</b> is the way people experience and express themselves <a href="/wiki/Human_sexual_activity" title="Human sexual activity">sexually</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cavendish_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cavendish-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ferrante_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ferrante-2">[2]</a></sup> This involves <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biological" title="Biological">biological</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Psychological" title="Psychological">psychological</a>, <a href="/wiki/Physical_intimacy" title="Physical intimacy">physical</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Erotic" title="Erotic">erotic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emotional_intimacy" title="Emotional intimacy">emotional</a>, <a href="/wiki/Social" title="Social">social</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Spirituality" title="Spirituality">spiritual</a> feelings and behaviors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-S._Greenberg_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-S._Greenberg-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bolin_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bolin-4">[4]</a></sup> Because it is a broad term, which has varied with historical contexts over time, it lacks a precise definition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bolin_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bolin-4">[4]</a></sup> The biological and physical aspects of sexuality largely concern the <a href="/wiki/Human_reproduction" title="Human reproduction">human reproductive functions</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Human_sexual_response_cycle" title="Human sexual response cycle">human sexual response cycle</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-S._Greenberg_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-S._Greenberg-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bolin_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-Bolin-4">[4]</a></sup>
</p><p>Someone's <a href="/wiki/Sexual_orientation" title="Sexual orientation">sexual orientation</a> is their pattern of sexual interest in the opposite or same sex.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AmPsycholAssn-whatis_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-AmPsycholAssn-whatis-5">[5]</a></sup> Physical and emotional aspects of sexuality include bonds between individuals that are expressed through profound feelings or physical manifestations of <a href="/wiki/Romance_(love)" title="Romance (love)">love</a>, trust, and care. Social aspects deal with the effects of human society on one's sexuality, while spirituality concerns an individual's spiritual connection with others. Sexuality also affects and is affected by cultural, political, legal, philosophical, <a href="/wiki/Morality" title="Morality">moral</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethical" title="Ethical">ethical</a>, and religious aspects of life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-S._Greenberg_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-S._Greenberg-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bolin_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-Bolin-4">[4]</a></sup>
</p><p>Interest in sexual activity typically increases when an individual reaches <a href="/wiki/Puberty" title="Puberty">puberty</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> Although no single theory on the cause of sexual orientation has yet gained widespread support, there is considerably more evidence supporting nonsocial causes of sexual orientation than social ones, especially for males. Hypothesized social causes are supported by only weak evidence, distorted by numerous confounding factors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bailey16_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bailey16-7">[7]</a></sup> This is further supported by cross-cultural evidence, because cultures that are tolerant of <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">homosexuality</a> do not have significantly higher rates of it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LeVay_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-LeVay-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Balthazart_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Balthazart-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p>Evolutionary perspectives on human coupling, reproduction and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reproduction_strategies" title="Reproduction strategies">reproduction strategies</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Social_learning_theory" title="Social learning theory">social learning theory</a> provide further views of sexuality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Sociocultural aspects of sexuality include <a href="/wiki/History_of_human_sexuality" title="History of human sexuality">historical developments</a> and <a href="/wiki/Religion_and_sexuality" title="Religion and sexuality">religious beliefs</a>. Some cultures have been described as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sexually_repressive" title="Sexually repressive">sexually repressive</a>. The study of sexuality also includes human identity within social groups, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sexually_transmitted_infections" title="Sexually transmitted infections">sexually transmitted infections</a> (STIs/STDs), and <a href="/wiki/Birth_control" title="Birth control">birth control</a> methods.
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style><div class="toclimit-3"><div aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading" class="toc" id="toc" role="navigation"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>
